style=\"width:33%;padding-left:0.25em\">\n<a href=\"/wiki/Marthad%27ilan_Yu%27nim\" title=\"Marthad'ilan Yu'nim\">Marthad'ilan Yu'nim</a> <a href=\"/wiki/Death_by_natural_causes\" class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Death by natural causes\">#</a><br><a href=\"/wiki/Imru%27_al-Qays\" class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Imru' al-Qays\">Imru' al-Qays</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan=\"3\" style=\"background-color:#C3D6EF;color:inherit;text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;font-size:110%;\">Units involved</th></tr><tr><td style=\"width:33%;border-right:1px dotted #aaa;\">\nTribal soldiers from Banu Taghlib</td><td style=\"width:33%;border-right:1px dotted #aaa;;padding-left:0.25em\">\nTribal soldiers from Banu Bakr</td><td style=\"width:33%;padding-left:0.25em\">\nAt least 500 Himyarite warriors</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Basus War</b> (often written <b>al-Basus War</b>; <a href=\"/wiki/Arabic_language\" class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Arabic language\">Arabic</a>: <span lang=\"ar\" dir=\"rtl\">حرب البسوس</span> <i>ḥarb al-basūs</i>) is a famous conflict narrative from the corpus of the a<i>yyām al-ʿarab</i> (<a href=\"/wiki/Days_of_the_Arabs\" title=\"Days of the Arabs\"><i>Days of the Arabs</i></a>), traditionally dated to late <a href=\"/wiki/Pre-Islamic_Arabia\" title=\"Pre-Islamic Arabia\">pre-Islamic Arabia</a> and showcasing the rivalry of the tribes of <a href=\"/wiki/Taghlib\" title=\"Taghlib\">Taghlib</a> and <a href=\"/wiki/Banu_Bakr\" title=\"Banu Bakr\">Bakr</a>. In  Arabic historical and literary tradition, it is portrayed as a forty-year tribal war triggered by the killing of a camel belonging to a woman named Basus. The story occupies an important place in Arabic literary culture as a famous <a href=\"/wiki/Aphorism\" title=\"Aphorism\">aphorism</a> warning against vendetta, kin-violence, and escalation. \n</p><p>Modern scholarship, however, increasingly treats the Basus War not as a single, prolonged historical war but as a composite and progressively elaborated narrative, likely originating in a limited skirmish, later expanded in scope, duration, and moral significance through oral poetry, genealogical rivalry, and <i>adab</i> literature. Early sources differ substantially on the sequence of events, the identities of participants, and even the basic motivations involved, suggesting that the narrative stabilized only gradually over time.<sup id=\"cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHussein2025_1-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHussein2025-1\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>1<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<meta property=\"mw:PageProp/toc\">\n<div class=\"mw-heading mw-heading2\"><h2 id=\"Background\">Background</h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a href=\"/w/index.php?title=Basus_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Background\"><span>edit</span></a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class=\"mw-default-size\" typeof=\"mw:File/Thumb\"><a href=\"/wiki/File:Qabr_Kulaib_ibn_Rabiah.jpg\" class=\"mw-file-description\"><img src=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Qabr_Kulaib_ibn_Rabiah.jpg/250px-Qabr_Kulaib_ibn_Rabiah.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"250\" height=\"141\" class=\"mw-file-element\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Qabr_Kulaib_ibn_Rabiah.jpg/500px-Qabr_Kulaib_ibn_Rabiah.jpg 2x\" data-file-width=\"2554\" data-file-height=\"1440\"></a><figcaption>The tomb of Kulaib ibn Rabiah located at Wadi Khaitan</figcaption></figure>\n<p>According to literary accounts, the conflict began when <a href=\"/wiki/Kulaib_ibn_Rabiah\" title=\"Kulaib ibn Rabiah\">Kulaib ibn Rabiah</a>, a leading figure of <a href=\"/wiki/Taghlib\" title=\"Taghlib\">Taghlib</a>, killed a camel belonging to Basus, a woman related to <a href=\"/wiki/Jassas_ibn_Murrah\" title=\"Jassas ibn Murrah\">Jassas ibn Murrah</a> of the <a href=\"/wiki/Banu_Shayban\" title=\"Banu Shayban\">Shayban</a> branch of <a href=\"/wiki/Banu_Bakr\" title=\"Banu Bakr\">Banu Bakr</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-2\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>2<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-:2_3-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-:2-3\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>3<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-:0_4-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-:0-4\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>4<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup> The lament of Basus, presented poetically, provoked Jassas to kill Kulayb, setting of off retaliatory violence between two tribes.<sup id=\"cite_ref-:2_3-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-:2-3\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>3<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-:0_4-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-:0-4\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>4<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class=\"mw-heading mw-heading2\"><h2 id=\"Course_of_conflict\">Course of conflict</h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a href=\"/w/index.php?title=Basus_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Course of conflict\"><span>edit</span></a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></div>\n<p>On a day known as <i>Yawm al-Hazr</i>, the Banu Taghlib carried out an assault against the Banu Shayban. They were victorious, and majority of the casualties were from the Banu Shayban. Then a few days later, the Banu Taghlib confronted the Arab tribe of <a href=\"/wiki/Zubaid\" title=\"Zubaid\">Zubaid</a>. No casualties were reported, and later on the Banu Taghlib continued their attacks on Banu Shayban, killing one of the important Banu Shayban members. Gradually, the whole group of Banu Bakr (including all subdivisions) participated in the war against Banu Taghlib. One of the first victories against Banu Taghlib was on a day known as <i>Yawm 'ala Istirad</i>, where a criminal from that tribe was killed.<sup id=\"cite_ref-:0_4-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-:0-4\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>4<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-:1_5-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-:1-5\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>5<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup> \n</p>\n<div class=\"mw-heading mw-heading2\"><h2 id=\"Ultimatum\">Ultimatum</h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a href=\"/w/index.php?title=Basus_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Ultimatum\"><span>edit</span></a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Some years later, some of the subdivisions of Banu Bakr pulled out from fighting. This angered the Bakry chief Uday ibn Murrah, who called out all those Bakrys who backed off. Internal dissent occurred amongst the Banu Bakr, but it was eventually resolved. The decision was to retreat and hold a session. Due to the high number of losses, the decision was made for them to retreat, reproduce and then go back to war. So they did, they attacked some forty years later by their fresh younger generations and that's why its referred to as the 40-year-war. It took them forty years to breed a new army and go back and finish off the battle with a final victory.<sup id=\"cite_ref-:0_4-3\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-:0-4\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>4<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-:1_5-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-:1-5\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>5<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class=\"mw-heading mw-heading3\"><h3 id=\"Himyarite_involvement\">Himyarite involvement</h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a href=\"/w/index.php?title=Basus_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Himyarite involvement\"><span>edit</span></a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The Himyarite ruler <a href=\"/wiki/Marthad%27ilan_Yu%27nim\" title=\"Marthad'ilan Yu'nim\">Marthad'ilan Yu'nim</a> dispatched at least five hundred soldiers to assist <a href=\"/wiki/Imru%27_al-Qays\" class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Imru' al-Qays\">Imru' al-Qays</a> in his mission to reunite the tribes of Taghlib and Banu Bakr, with the goal of fighting against the <a href=\"/wiki/Banu_Asad\" title=\"Banu Asad\">Banu Asad</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-6\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-6\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>6<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class=\"mw-heading mw-heading2\"><h2 id=\"Aftermath_and_end_of_conflict\">Aftermath and end of conflict</h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a href=\"/w/index.php?title=Basus_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Aftermath and end of conflict\"><span>edit</span></a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></div>\n<p>After the Banu Taghlib had suffered several defeats, their leading commander, <a href=\"/wiki/Abu_Layla_al-Muhalhel\" class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Abu Layla al-Muhalhel\">Abu Layla al-Muhalhel</a> fled but was captured by a <a href=\"/wiki/Madhhaj\" class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Madhhaj\">Madh'hiji</a> tribe in <a href=\"/wiki/South_Arabia\" title=\"South Arabia\">South of Arabia</a> and forced to marry a woman from that tribe. The Banu Taghlib tribe eventually dispersed into the lands of <a href=\"/wiki/Iraq\" title=\"Iraq\">Iraq</a>, where they stayed for the rest of their lives. The fighting soon died down, and by the 530s, the war had already ended.<sup id=\"cite_ref-:0_4-4\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-:0-4\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>4<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-:1_5-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-:1-5\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>5<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-7\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-7\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>7<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Banu Taghlib were the victors of the war at first since they killed most of the Banu Bakr forces. But they eventually capitulated after forty years as Banu Bakr came for retaliation and started the killing again. The poetry that came along the war is documented specifically until our time. <sup id=\"cite_ref-8\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-8\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>8<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class=\"mw-heading mw-heading2\"><h2 id=\"In_popular_culture\">In popular culture</h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a href=\"/w/index.php?title=Basus_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: In popular culture\"><span>edit</span></a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The Basus War is referenced as an <a href=\"/wiki/Aphorism\" title=\"Aphorism\">aphorism</a> against having grudges, family feud, vendettas and violent rivalries.<sup id=\"cite_ref-9\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-9\"><span class=\"cite-bracket\">[</span>9<span class=\"cite-bracket\">]</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class=\"mw-heading mw-heading2\"><h2 id=\"See_also\">See also</h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a href=\"/w/index.php?title=Basus_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: See also\"><span>edit</span></a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li><a href=\"/wiki/Battle_of_Dhat_Irq\" title=\"Battle of Dhat Irq\">Battle of Dhat Irq</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"/wiki/Yawm_al-Nakhla\" title=\"Yawm al-Nakhla\">Yawm al-Nakhla</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"/wiki/Dahis_and_al-Ghubra\" class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Dahis and al-Ghubra\">Dahis and al-Ghubra</a></li></ul>\n<div class=\"mw-heading mw-heading2\"><h2
